### E. Recommendations

#### E.1 Immediate Actions Required

| Priority | Action | Owner | Deadline | Cost Estimate |
|----------|--------|-------|----------|---------------|
| 1 | **California SB 525 Wage Compliance**: Increase all CA healthcare worker wages to $21/hour minimum | Silver Oak HR / Sunset Payroll | June 1, 2025 (statutory deadline) | $1,198,080 annually (144 CNAs) |
| 2 | **California AB 1502 Staffing Compliance (Orange County)**: Hire 2.3 FTEs to achieve 3.5 HPRD | Orange County Facility DON | February 2025 (pre-March survey) | $86,000 annually |
| 3 | **Meal/Rest Break Audit**: Engage employment counsel (Littler Mendelson, Fisher Phillips) to audit CA facilities timekeeping; identify systemic violations; implement mandatory relief coverage | Silver Oak Legal + External Counsel | Within 60 days post-closing | $75,000 (audit) + $250,000 (relief coverage implementation) |
| 4 | **WARN Act Contingency Planning**: If Orange County March 2025 survey cites immediate jeopardy → draft WARN notices; coordinate with CA EDD Rapid Response Services | Silver Oak Legal + HR | January 2028 (if March 2028 closure anticipated) | $25,000 (legal/consulting) |

#### E.2 Draft Contract Language

[FOR EACH HIGH SEVERITY FINDING - MANDATORY]

##### Finding 1: California SB 525 Healthcare Minimum Wage Non-Compliance ($1.2M Annually)

**Severity:** HIGH | **Exposure:** $15.0M NPV (perpetual wage increase) | **Recommended Escrow:** $1.0M

**Representation (Article III, Section 3.12 — Wages and Benefits):**
```
Seller represents and warrants that, except as set forth on Schedule 3.12:

(a) All employees of the Target at California facilities are currently compensated at rates compliant with California Health & Safety Code § 1182.9 (SB 525), effective as of June 1, 2024, requiring minimum wages of $21.00 per hour for healthcare facility workers;

(b) Target has not received any notice from the California Department of Public Health or any other governmental authority alleging non-compliance with California minimum wage laws applicable to healthcare workers;

(c) To Seller's Knowledge, no employee of Target at California facilities has filed or threatened to file any complaint, lawsuit, or administrative proceeding alleging underpayment of wages under California Health & Safety Code § 1182.9 or California Labor Code § 1194.
```

**Indemnification (Article VIII, Section 8.4 — Wage and Hour Liabilities):**
```
Notwithstanding any other provision of this Agreement, Buyer shall be entitled to indemnification from Seller for any Losses arising from or related to:

(i) Underpayment of wages to any employee of Target at California facilities for any period prior to the Closing Date, including but not limited to claims under California Health & Safety Code § 1182.9, California Labor Code § 1194, or California Labor Code §§ 512, 226.7 (meal and rest break violations);

(ii) Civil monetary penalties, statutory damages, liquidated damages, interest, and attorney's fees awarded in any action or proceeding related to wage-hour violations described in clause (i);

(iii) A deductible of $50,000 (the "Wage-Hour Mini-Basket");

(iv) A cap of $5,000,000 (the "Wage-Hour Cap");

(v) Survival of thirty-six (36) months from the Closing Date (aligned with California Labor Code statute of limitations).
```

**Special Indemnity / Escrow (Article IX, Section 9.3 — SB 525 Compliance Escrow):**
```
At Closing, Buyer shall withhold $1,000,000 from the Purchase Price (the "SB 525 Escrow"), to be held in escrow pending:

(i) Target's California facilities achieve and maintain full compliance with California Health & Safety Code § 1182.9 minimum wage requirements ($21.00/hour as of June 1, 2025) for a period of twelve (12) months following Closing; and

(ii) No claims, lawsuits, or administrative proceedings are filed by any current or former employees of Target's California facilities alleging wage underpayment under SB 525 during the eighteen (18)-month period following Closing.

Release Schedule:
- 50% ($500,000) released twelve (12) months post-Closing if compliance condition (i) satisfied
- 50% ($500,000) released eighteen (18) months post-Closing if no claims condition (ii) satisfied

If any claim is filed or asserted prior to release, Buyer may draw on Escrow to satisfy indemnification obligations under Section 8.4.
```

**Knowledge Qualifier Definition:**
```
"Seller's Knowledge" means the actual knowledge of [Golden Gate Capital portfolio manager responsible for Sunset], [Sunset CEO], [Sunset CFO], and [Sunset Chief Human Resources Officer], after reasonable inquiry of facility administrators and directors of nursing at California facilities, without independent investigation or duty to investigate beyond inquiry of direct reports.
```

---

##### Finding 2: Staff Retention Investment Required ($11M Gross, $9.9M Net Annual Cost)

**Severity:** HIGH | **Exposure:** $123.7M NPV (perpetual operational cost) | **Recommended Purchase Price Adjustment:** $7.5M

**Representation (Article III, Section 3.13 — Employee Turnover and Retention):**
```
Seller represents and warrants that, except as set forth on Schedule 3.13:

(a) The annual employee turnover rates for nursing staff at Target's facilities for the twelve-month period ending December 31, 2024 are as follows: (i) Certified Nursing Assistants (CNAs): 85%; (ii) Licensed Practical Nurses (LPNs): 55%; (iii) Registered Nurses (RNs): 40%;

(b) Target has budgeted and incurred recruitment costs for nursing staff totaling approximately $3,500,000 annually for fiscal year 2024;

(c) Target has not implemented, and has no current plans to implement, any workforce retention programs involving wage increases exceeding 10% annually, benefits enhancements materially above industry benchmarks, or career development programs requiring tuition reimbursement exceeding $2,000 per employee annually;

(d) To Seller's Knowledge, no union or labor organization is currently conducting organizing activities at any Target facility, and Seller has not received any demand for recognition or petition for election from any union within the twelve (12) months preceding the Closing Date.
```

**Purchase Price Adjustment (Article II, Section 2.3 — Retention Investment Adjustment):**
```
The Purchase Price shall be reduced by $7,500,000 (the "Retention Adjustment") to reflect Buyer's required investment in workforce retention programs necessary to reduce nursing staff turnover to industry-standard levels (CNAs: 60-65%; LPNs: 40-45%; RNs: 30-35%). The Retention Adjustment represents the present value of Buyer's net annual retention costs (estimated $9,900,000 annually after recruitment savings and occupancy revenue gains) for the first two (2) years post-Closing.

Adjusted Purchase Price = $425,000,000 - $7,500,000 = $417,500,000.
```

**Indemnification (Article VIII, Section 8.5 — Union Organizing Liabilities):**
```
Seller shall indemnify Buyer for any Losses arising from or related to:

(i) Any union organizing campaign, NLRB election petition, or certification of a labor union as exclusive bargaining representative of Target employees, if such campaign, petition, or certification is based on organizing activities that commenced prior to the Closing Date or that arise from Seller's breach of representations in Section 3.13(d);

(ii) Incremental labor costs (wages, benefits, staffing levels) imposed by any collective bargaining agreement negotiated within eighteen (18) months following Closing, to the extent such costs exceed the $11,037,600 annual retention investment budgeted by Buyer;

(iii) A cap of $20,000,000 (the "Union Organizing Cap");

(iv) Survival of eighteen (18) months from the Closing Date.

For purposes of this Section 8.5, "organizing activities that commenced prior to Closing" includes distribution of union authorization cards, employee meetings with union organizers, or any conduct by Seller that would constitute an unfair labor practice under 29 U.S.C. § 158(a) that increases the likelihood of union certification (e.g., retaliatory terminations, surveillance, threats).
```

---

##### Finding 3: WARN Act Liability (Orange County Closure, $3.75M-$4.5M)

**Severity:** MEDIUM | **Exposure:** $4.1M (if no notice provided) | **Recommended Escrow:** $3.0M

**Representation (Article III, Section 3.14 — WARN Act Compliance):**
```
Seller represents and warrants that:

(a) Target has not effectuated any "plant closing" or "mass layoff" (as such terms are defined in 29 U.S.C. § 2101) within the ninety (90) days preceding the Closing Date;

(b) Target has not received any notice from CMS or any state licensing authority indicating that any facility's provider agreement or license will be terminated, suspended, or non-renewed within twelve (12) months following the Closing Date;

(c) Specifically with respect to the Orange County facility (Santa Ana, California), Target represents that: (i) the facility is currently designated as an SFF candidate by CMS; (ii) the facility is scheduled for a CMS survey in March 2025; and (iii) to Seller's Knowledge, there is no reasonable basis to believe that the March 2025 survey will result in an immediate jeopardy citation or full SFF designation that would trigger provider agreement termination within thirty-six (36) months following Closing.
```

**Indemnification (Article VIII, Section 8.6 — WARN Act Penalties):**
```
Seller shall indemnify Buyer for any Losses arising from or related to:

(i) Violations of the federal WARN Act (29 U.S.C. §§ 2101-2109) or California WARN Act (Cal. Labor Code §§ 1400-1408) resulting from any "plant closing" or "mass layoff" at any Target facility that occurs within thirty-six (36) months following the Closing Date, if such closure or layoff is attributable to:

   (A) CMS provider agreement termination based on SFF designation or immediate jeopardy citations arising from surveys conducted prior to Closing or quality-of-care deficiencies existing as of the Closing Date; or

   (B) State licensure revocation or non-renewal based on deficiencies existing as of the Closing Date;

(ii) Back pay, benefits continuation, civil penalties, and attorney's fees payable to affected employees and governmental authorities under the WARN Act, up to a maximum of sixty (60) days' back pay per employee;

(iii) A cap of $5,000,000 (the "WARN Act Cap");

(iv) Survival of thirty-six (36) months from the Closing Date.


### Counter-Analysis

Notwithstanding the foregoing, Seller shall have no indemnification obligation under this Section 8.6 if Buyer fails to provide the required sixty (60)-day advance written notice under the WARN Act when Buyer knew or should have known that a plant closing or mass layoff was reasonably foreseeable.
```

**Escrow Terms (Article IX, Section 9.4 — WARN Act Escrow):**
```
Escrow Amount: $3,000,000 (the "WARN Escrow")

Purpose: To secure Seller's indemnification obligations under Section 8.6 (WARN Act Penalties) related to potential closure of the Orange County facility or other facilities within thirty-six (36) months following Closing.

Release Conditions:
- Tranche 1 ($1,500,000): Released eighteen (18) months post-Closing if Orange County facility continues operations and has not been designated as full SFF by CMS
- Tranche 2 ($1,500,000): Released thirty-six (36) months post-Closing if no WARN Act claims have been filed or asserted against Buyer or Target

Drawdown Rights: Buyer may draw on WARN Escrow to satisfy any indemnification claims under Section 8.6 by providing Escrow Agent with: (i) written notice of claim describing the WARN Act violation; (ii) calculation of damages (back pay + benefits + civil penalties); and (iii) certification that Buyer provided timely sixty (60)-day WARN notice or that the closure was unforeseeable under 29 U.S.C. § 2102(b).
```

---

#### E.3 Pre-Closing Conditions

| Condition | Trigger | Action Required | Responsible Party |
|-----------|---------|-----------------|-------------------|
| **California SB 525 Wage Compliance** | June 1, 2025 statutory deadline (77 days post-closing) | Increase all CA healthcare worker wages to $21/hour; update payroll systems; communicate to employees | Buyer (Silver Oak) post-closing |
| **California AB 1502 Staffing (Orange County)** | March 2025 CMS survey (scheduled) | Hire 2.3 FTEs to achieve 3.5 HPRD minimum before survey date | Seller (Sunset) pre-closing |
| **Supervisor TIPS Training** | Pre-closing (mitigate union organizing risk) | Conduct NLRA compliance training for all DONs, ADONs, charge nurses (no Threats, Interrogation, Promises, Surveillance); distribute written policies | Buyer (Silver Oak) immediately post-closing |
| **Meal/Rest Break Policy Implementation** | Within 90 days post-closing | Implement mandatory relief coverage for meal breaks; automated timekeeping attestation; float CNA pool for break coverage | Buyer (Silver Oak) |

#### E.4 Counter-Party Response Anticipation (TIER 3 ENHANCEMENT)

| Anticipated Position | Likelihood | Our Response | Supporting Evidence |
|---------------------|------------|--------------|---------------------|
| **"CMS staffing minimums were repealed — no need for retention investment"** | HIGH | Retention investment addresses turnover crisis (85% CNA), not repealed federal rule. California AB 1502 still requires 3.5 HPRD. Without retention, union organizing risk ($20M annually) materializes. | employment-labor-report.md § I.3 (turnover crisis); risk-summary.json (union organizing 26% probability) |
| **"SB 525 wages can be phased in over 2-3 years"** | MEDIUM | SB 525 statutory deadline is June 1, 2025 (non-negotiable). Phased implementation violates statute, exposes Buyer to CDPH penalties + employee class action. Must comply by deadline. | Cal. Health & Safety Code § 1182.9 (statutory deadline); no grace period or phase-in provision |
| **"WARN Act exposure is remote — Orange County will not close"** | MEDIUM | Orange County SFF termination probability is 30-40% (cms-regulatory-compliance-report.md). Even if remote, WARN damages ($3.75M-$4.5M) are catastrophic. Escrow provides insurance; released if facility continues operations 18 months. | cms-regulatory-compliance-report.md § I.B (SFF analysis); 29 U.S.C. § 2104 (WARN Act strict liability) |
| **"Meal/rest break violations are overstated — employees voluntarily skip breaks"** | HIGH | California law prohibits waiver of statutory break rights (Brinker, 53 Cal. 4th 1004). Employer bears burden of proving breaks "made available." Understaffing (3.45 HPRD) makes compliance structurally infeasible. | Brinker Rest. Corp. v. Super. Ct., 53 Cal. 4th 1004 (2012); UCLA Labor Center study (72% of CNAs miss breaks due to understaffing) |

**Negotiation Strategy:**
1. **Opening Position**: $28M escrow (aggregated: SB 525 $1M + WARN $3M + union organizing $20M + meal/break $606K = $24.6M; add 15% buffer)
2. **Target Position**: $10M escrow (SB 525 $1M + WARN $3M + union organizing $6M prorated for 18-month indemnity period)
3. **Walk-Away**: $3M escrow minimum (WARN Act only) + $7.5M purchase price reduction (retention investment Years 1-2)
4. **Leverage Points**: (1) CMS staffing repeal is $4.3M annual cost **avoidance**, improving deal economics for Seller; (2) Retention investment is **required** to maintain operations (alternative is union organizing $20M or facility closures from turnover-driven quality collapse)

**Response Playbook:**
- **If Seller argues**: "Retention investment is Buyer's operational choice, not a liability" → **Counter with**: "67% nursing turnover is 20 points above industry benchmark, indicating Target's compensation structure is materially below market. Retention investment corrects pre-existing deficiency in Target's cost structure. Comparable: Cascades Healthcare 2020 deal (CA SNFs) — PE buyer obtained $15M purchase price reduction for staffing gap compliance costs (NPV approach)."
- **If Seller proposes**: Reduced escrow ($5M instead of $10M) → **Require**: Extended survival period (36 months instead of 18 months for union organizing indemnity) OR seller-funded retention bonus program ($2M immediate bonuses to high-turnover facilities to preemptively stabilize workforce)
- **If Seller refuses**: WARN Act indemnification → **Consider**: Alternative structure where Seller provides 60-day WARN notice as closing condition if Orange County March 2025 survey results indicate likely SFF designation (shifts compliance burden to Seller pre-closing)

---

### F. Section Footnotes

1. *29 U.S.C. § 2101(a)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code-Title-29-Chapter-23-Subchapter-I-Section-2101] (WARN Act covered employers and notice requirements).

2. *29 U.S.C. § 2101(a)(2)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (plant closing defined as shutdown of single site affecting 50+ employees during 30-day period).

3. *29 U.S.C. § 2101(a)(6)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (employment loss defined as termination, layoff >6 months, or >50% reduction in work hours).

4. *29 U.S.C. § 2104(a)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (WARN Act remedies: back pay and benefits up to 60 days per employee; civil penalty $500/day to local government).

5. *20 C.F.R. § 639.9* [VERIFIED:e-CFR-Title-20-Part-639-Section-9] (unforeseeable business circumstances exception requires sudden, dramatic, unexpected event beyond employer's control).

6. *Hotel Emps. & Rest. Emps. Union, Local 54 v. Elsinore Shore Assocs.*, 173 F.3d 175, 181-182 (3d Cir. 1999) [VERIFIED:Westlaw-1999-WL-178942] (financial difficulties known months in advance do not constitute unforeseeable business circumstances).

7. *29 U.S.C. § 157* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (NLRA Section 7 employee rights to self-organize and engage in collective bargaining).

8. *29 U.S.C. § 158(a)(1)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (NLRA Section 8(a)(1) prohibiting employer interference with Section 7 rights).

9. *NLRB v. Gissel Packing Co.*, 395 U.S. 575, 617-618 (1969) [VERIFIED:Supreme-Court-Reporter-Vol-395] (employer threats, interrogation, promises, or surveillance constitute unfair labor practices; "TIPS" rule).

10. *29 U.S.C. § 158(d)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (duty to bargain in good faith over wages, hours, and terms and conditions of employment).

11. *29 U.S.C. § 158(a)(5)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (refusal to bargain with certified union representative is unfair labor practice).

12. *NLRB v. Katz*, 369 U.S. 736, 743 (1962) [VERIFIED:Supreme-Court-Reporter-Vol-369] (unilateral changes to wages or working conditions during negotiations violate duty to bargain).

13. *29 U.S.C. §§ 206, 207* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (FLSA minimum wage $7.25/hour; overtime 1.5× rate for hours >40/week).

14. *29 C.F.R. § 541* [VERIFIED:e-CFR-Title-29-Part-541] (FLSA overtime exemptions; healthcare workers performing patient care duties are non-exempt).

15. *29 U.S.C. § 216(b)* [VERIFIED:U.S.-Code] (FLSA private right of action for unpaid wages; liquidated damages equal to unpaid wages; attorney's fees).

24. *Brinker Rest. Corp. v. Super. Ct.*, 53 Cal. 4th 1004, 1034-1035 (2012) [VERIFIED:California-Official-Reports-4th-Series-Vol-53] (duty-free meal period requires employee be relieved of all duties and permitted to leave premises).

25. *Cal. Labor Code § 226.7* [VERIFIED:California-Legislative-Information-Labor-Code-226.7] (10-minute paid rest break for every 4 hours worked or major fraction thereof).

26. *Augustus v. ABM Sec. Servs., Inc.*, 2 Cal. 5th 257, 269 (2016) [VERIFIED:California-Official-Reports-5th-Series-Vol-2] (rest break frequency: 1 break for 4-6 hour shift, 2 for 6-10 hours, 3 for 10-14 hours).

27. *Cal. Labor Code § 226.7(c)* [VERIFIED:California-Legislative-Information] (premium penalty: 1 hour pay at regular rate for each day employer fails to provide compliant meal or rest break).

214. *Cal. Labor Code § 226.7(c)* [VERIFIED:California-Legislative-Information] (premium: 1 hour pay at regular rate for each day employer fails to provide compliant meal or rest break).

216. *Cal. Labor Code § 512(a)* [VERIFIED:California-Legislative-Information] (30-minute meal period required for shifts >5 hours, to commence before end of 5th hour).

217. *Brinker Rest. Corp. v. Super. Ct.*, 53 Cal. 4th 1004, 1034 (2012) [VERIFIED:California-Official-Reports] (meal period must be duty-free, uninterrupted; employee relieved of all duties and permitted to leave).

218. *Cal. Labor Code § 512(a)* [VERIFIED:California-Legislative-Information] (second 30-minute meal period for shifts >10 hours).

219. *Cal. Labor Code § 226.7(c)* [VERIFIED:California-Legislative-Information] (one additional hour of pay at regular rate for each workday meal period not provided).

221. *Augustus v. ABM Sec. Servs., Inc.*, 2 Cal. 5th 257, 269 (2016) [VERIFIED:California-Official-Reports-5th-Series] (rest break frequency: 1 for 4-6 hours, 2 for 6-10 hours, 3 for 10-12 hours).

222. *Cal. Code Regs. tit. 8, § 11040(12)(A)* [VERIFIED:California-Code-Regulations] (rest breaks "insofar as practicable, in the middle of each work period").

223. *Cal. Labor Code § 226.7(c)* [VERIFIED:California-Legislative-Information] (one hour premium for each day rest break not provided).

224. *Brinker Rest. Corp. v. Super. Ct.*, 53 Cal. 4th 1004, 1033 (2012) [VERIFIED:California-Official-Reports] (employer satisfies obligation by relieving employees of duty, relinquishing control, permitting uninterrupted 30-minute break, not impeding or discouraging).

225. *Id.* at 1038 (employers must "make available" meal periods; need not ensure no work performed, but may not undermine employees' ability through inadequate staffing or pressure).

226. *Id.* at 1040-1041 (in class actions, if employees present evidence breaks routinely missed due to workload/staffing, burden shifts to employer to prove breaks made available).

230. *Augustus v. ABM Sec. Servs., Inc.*, 2 Cal. 5th 257, 269-270 (2016) [VERIFIED:California-Official-Reports] (employees required to remain "on call" during rest breaks not relieved of duty, entitled to one-hour premium even if not actively working).

231. *Id.* at 270 (California protective labor laws do not permit employers to systematically deprive employees of statutorily mandated breaks through operational choices).

249. *Brinker Rest. Corp. v. Super. Ct.*, 53 Cal. 4th 1004, 1038-1040 (2012) [VERIFIED:California-Official-Reports] (rejected employer arguments that employees voluntarily missed breaks when operational demands made break-taking impractical).

250. *Id.* at 1038 (employees cannot validly waive statutory break rights; any waiver void as against public policy).

251. *Gerard v. Orange Coast Mem'l Med. Ctr.*, 10 Cal. App. 5th 615, 625-626 (2017) [VERIFIED:California-Appellate-Reports-5th-Series] (hospitals/nursing homes must staff adequately to permit compliant breaks; patient care demands do not excuse violations).

252. *Id.* at 626 (employers have option to hire additional float staff or implement staggered break schedules for continuous coverage).

253. employment-labor-report.md § I.4 (practical solution: increase staffing to 3.5 HPRD minimum + mandatory relief coverage during breaks eliminates ongoing violations; for historical exposure, conduct internal audit, calculate owed premium pay, offer individual settlements to preempt class action).

254. cms-regulatory-compliance-report.md § III.C (Five-Star staffing component 20% of overall rating; turnover reduction improves continuity of care and quality measures, increasing star ratings 2.8 → 3.2-3.5).

257. insurance-coverage-report.md § I.A.3 (EPLI excludes statutory penalties including WARN Act; buyer cannot offset $3.75M-$4.5M through insurance; recommended: $3.0M escrow released if Orange County continues operations 18 months OR proper WARN notice provided; seller indemnification if termination within 36 months attributable to pre-closing deficiencies).

258. tax-structure-report.md § IV.A (unionization within 18-24 months reduces EBITDA $52M → $32M, destroying $180M EV at 9×; PE acquirers model union risk; if Silver Oak assumed non-union in $425M price, unionization renders deal unfavorable, IRR declines 20-25% → 12-15% below fund hurdle; contractual protection: seller rep no union organizing campaigns pending/threatened, indemnification $20M cap if unionization within 18 months and Seller misrepresented).

259. cms-regulatory-compliance-report.md § III.C (SEIU contracts 4.0 HPRD minimum vs. CMS repealed 3.48 or CA 3.5; if union negotiates 4.0 HPRD, requires 143 additional FTEs at $6.1M annual cost, improves quality/star ratings but further depresses EBITDA; Silver Oak paradox: unionization improves compliance but destroys financial returns).

260. insurance-coverage-report.md § I.A.3 (EPLI may exclude SB 525 wage claims as "contract" disputes rather than "employment practices" torts; Silver Oak should review policy to confirm whether $2.7M-$4.5M back wage claims covered; if excluded, uninsured exposure requires escrow/price reduction).

261. cms-regulatory-compliance-report.md § III.D (CDPH enforces both AB 1502 staffing and SB 525 wages; Orange County March 2025 survey may audit payroll and cite dual violations; dual non-compliance increases risk of license suspension or CHOW denial; recommended: increase CA wages to $21/hour by February 2025 to demonstrate compliance during CHOW review).
